{"type":"reasoning","timestamp":1784499958204,"sessionID":"ses_083846643ffer2NQ0M0xWDVIbC","part":{"id":"prt_f7c7c6064001iELLYFhrVjCqWJ","messageID":"msg_f7c7c5e37001L7j8Hc0gFg3ni9","sessionID":"ses_083846643ffer2NQ0M0xWDVIbC","type":"reasoning","text":"\nNow I understand the issue fully. Looking at lines 1229-1233:\n\n```python\npool_ipc_handle=(\n    self.cudaipc_mmfeature_pool._pool_ipc_handle\n    if _IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE\n    else None\n),\n```\n\nWhen `SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE` is `False` (the default), the `pool_ipc_handle` is `None`. This means the tensor goes through the non-pooled IPC path. In the non-pooled path, the sender creates an IPC handle for each tensor, but under high concurrency the memory backing that handle can be freed/recycled by the memory pool before the receiver has reconstructed the tensor from the handle.\n\nWhen `SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE` is `True`, the sender shares a single pool-level IPC handle. The receiver caches the opened storage from this pool handle, so the memory stays alive as long as the pool exists. This prevents the stale pointer issue because the pool memory is never freed while the server is running.\n\n\nNow I need to implement the fix by setting `SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE=1` in the launch script and writing the analysis to `/app/analysis.json`.\n","time":{"start":1784499953764,"end":1784499958199}}}

Without `SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE`, each tensor gets its own IPC handle (non-pooled path at `cuda_ipc_transport_utils.py:488`). When the pool recycles that buffer, the receiver gets a stale device pointer → `HIP error: invalid device pointer` → scheduler crash.\n\n**Fix:** Set `SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE=1` in the launch script. This makes `base_processor.py:1229-1231` share a single pool-level IPC handle and cache the opened storage on the receiver side, so the underlying buffer never gets recycled while the server runs. The CUDA IPC multimodal transport stays enabled.","time":{"start":1784499969244,"end":1784499972566}}}
